Next story: US-001

## Codebase Patterns
- Stories are dependency ordered; document planned commands explicitly when their workspace/tooling lands later, and do not invent unconfirmed configuration defaults.
- Dependency installation, dependency changes, configuration changes, and database migrations require confirmation before execution.
- Local Compose data services bind to `127.0.0.1`; PostgreSQL is the only default service and future-only services must use explicit profiles.
- Project-local skills live under `.opencode/.opencode/skills`; they reference root `AGENTS.md`, use Bun scripts with Vitest, and report unavailable later-story tooling instead of creating it early.
- Workspace packages use the `@gamenight-bingo/*` namespace, extend `tsconfig.base.json`, and expose only compileable source entry points until their dependency-ordered implementation stories land; root workspaces are restricted to exactly `apps/*` and `packages/*`, and new package directories under them must be added to the validated workspace contract.
- Run `bun run test:workspace-boundaries` after workspace-manifest or domain-import changes; the TypeScript AST guard checks static, type-only, dynamic, direct CommonJS (including TypeScript-transparent and comma loader expressions), JSDoc, and triple-slash references with normalized path separators without matching ordinary comments or strings.
- Boundary parsing must use the source file's actual script kind and fail closed on syntax errors; workspace checks also require real `tsc` scripts without strictness downgrades, prohibit shared/domain module aliases, `rootDirs`, and `moduleSuffixes`, constrain relative source and root/nested package-resolution targets to `packages/domain/src`, and reject source/reference symlinks across TypeScript declaration and JavaScript-extension resolution candidates plus escaping absolute, file-URL, relative, type-reference, file-reference, and AMD dependency paths.
- Workspace typechecks must cover every discovered `src` file without inherited or implicit exclusions, verified against TypeScript's parsed effective file set, and must reject all parsed configuration diagnostics while retaining effective `noEmit` with `outDir`/`declarationDir` outside `src`; domain source also rejects JavaScript and `@ts-nocheck`. Shared/domain TypeScript configuration cannot inherit or synthesize implicit module imports, and domain bare imports plus package-valued type/AMD directives must be Node built-ins, self-references, or declared dependencies without traversal segments and validated against forbidden runtime or type-package aliases.
- Keep intentional ESLint, Prettier, TypeScript, Vitest, React Testing Library, and Playwright failures under `tests/fixtures/quality`; normal checks exclude them, while `bun run test:quality-tooling` requires each tool to fail for its expected diagnostic rather than accepting any nonzero exit.
- Vitest discovery is limited to repository `apps`, `packages`, and `tests` paths, explicitly excludes nested `node_modules` reached through Bun workspace links, runs TS tests in Node and TSX tests in jsdom, and leaves `tests/e2e` to the separate `bun run test:e2e` command.
- Runtime entry points pass `process.env` to `parseRuntimeConfig` from `packages/contracts`; downstream and domain code consume the immutable parsed type rather than reading environment state directly, and startup subprocess tests isolate environment/module state.
- After workspace dependency manifests change, run `bun install` to refresh `bun.lock`, then verify reproducibility with `bun install --frozen-lockfile`.
- Versioned Zod wire contracts live under `packages/contracts/src/v1`; every nested object is strict, top-level messages carry `schemaVersion`, identifiers and active-lobby sequences are branded, client commands contain intent rather than authoritative state, and authorized snapshots structurally omit credentials, foreign cards, future draws, prior-round history, and active event history. Lobby-wide sequences belong only on messages delivered to every authorized lobby consumer; private-only events omit them, acknowledgements declare their scope, and snapshot refinements enforce cross-object roster/state consistency.
- `docs/bingo-pattern-catalog.md` inventories source diagrams as `p1/dNN` in reading order with exact, flexible-example, or alias modes and tested 5x5 source masks; its generated core section is parity-tested from `packages/patterns/src/catalog.ts` rather than maintaining a second runtime mask source.
- Domain randomization accepts injected `CryptographicRandomBytes`; runtime adapters own the secure byte source, deterministic tests inject seeded bytes, and bounded integer selection uses rejection sampling rather than biased modulo reduction.
- Runtime pattern definitions store every accepted required-cell arrangement as a 5x5 mask: One Line has 12 line masks, Two Lines has all 66 distinct line-pair unions, exact patterns retain one untransformed source mask, and matching always satisfies index 12 as the free center.
- Exact generated Markdown parity blocks use `prettier-ignore` markers around the generated boundaries so formatting cannot silently rewrite canonical generator output.
- Source review records map every PDF diagram to its runtime ID and disposition (`exact-mask-match`, `flexible-rule-example`, or `source-alias`), record all 25 cells reviewed, and parity-test exact records against canonical runtime masks without duplicating masks in the review table.
- Pattern preview galleries derive a normalized model from `patternCatalog`; flexible-rule source examples live with the canonical pattern source, committed JSON goldens cover every runtime selection, and standalone generated HTML is parity-tested and isolated from Prettier with an exact-node ignore marker.
- Category preview pages reuse the source-filtered canonical preview model and shared renderer while exposing category-specific creation/generation functions, committed goldens, and standalone HTML paths.
- Approved theme IDs, moodboards, semantic color/motion roles, and accessibility policy live canonically in `packages/themes`; selectors and generated Markdown/HTML review documents derive from that catalog, while contrast tests cover authored text at 4.5:1 and non-text boundaries/indicators/focus at 3:1.
- Complete pattern audits join all PDF inventory/review rows to runtime IDs, aliases, exact or flexible mask parity, approved identity/mask constraints, and the combined category preview goldens; mutation tests must prove each audit failure category remains fail-closed.
- Domain transitions return discriminated stable errors for expected state rejection and throw `RangeError` only for malformed internal values such as invalid counts, timestamps, or durations.
- Prisma 7 is confined to `packages/database`; `bun run db:generate` creates the ignored client during install, while repository interfaces expose durable aggregate state without exporting Prisma types.
- PostgreSQL-only partial indexes, checks, and composite foreign keys live in append-only migration SQL; the durable schema keeps one current round per lobby so round cards, marks, private draw order, calls, winners, events, and command results cascade without prior-round history.
- Database integration tests require an explicitly approved, migrated PostgreSQL 16 `TEST_DATABASE_URL`; the generic Vitest run skips them when the variable is absent.
- Serializable command transactions lock and scope work to one lobby, check persisted command results before mutation, and use bounded observable retries; callbacks may rerun only after rollback and must have no external effects, while only fresh active-lobby commits return a broadcastable event.
- PostgreSQL concurrency tests must coordinate actual transaction overlap before asserting Serializable retries; observing the second command waiting on the lobby fence avoids flaky assumptions about `Promise.all` scheduling. Lock-coordination harnesses must roll back and release checked-out clients in `finally` blocks and await blocked operations during cleanup so synchronization failures cannot hang the suite.
- Retry classification scans nested Prisma/adapter `cause`, `meta`, and `driverAdapterError` metadata before falling back to generic conflict codes; PostgreSQL `40P01` deadlocks take precedence over outer Prisma `P2034` wrappers so telemetry stays accurate.
- Active lobby creation goes through `LobbyStateRepository.createActive`: generate each candidate outside retryable transactions, serialize PostgreSQL admission before counting waiting/active lobbies, and retry only active-code collisions so capacity cannot be oversubscribed.
- Normalize usernames at the trusted reservation boundary by rejecting Unicode control/format characters, trimming and collapsing Unicode whitespace, applying NFC, enforcing the 128-character display/key limit, then lowercasing for lobby-scoped uniqueness; serialize reservations on the lobby row before checking names and configured capacity.
- Participant session credentials use 32 injected cryptographic bytes encoded as unpadded base64url; hash the exact encoded token with SHA-256 before persistence, return it only through a Secure/HttpOnly/SameSite=Strict lobby-path cookie, and resolve identity through a narrow active-lobby plus hash lookup rather than a full aggregate or client-supplied participant ID.
- Same-device session lifecycle transitions share the active-lobby transaction fence and sample their repository clock after acquiring it on every retry: disconnect stores one durable deadline, rejoin-status sweeps expiry before cookie validation, `now >= rejoinUntil` atomically expires due credentials and departs a slot only when no valid sibling remains, timely rejoin clears lifecycle timestamps while invalidating siblings, and persistence derives waiting eligibility for new active-round joins.
- Next.js consumes the workspace's raw TypeScript packages through Webpack with a `.js` extension alias because their Node ESM source specifiers intentionally name emitted `.js` files; keep `.next` output ignored by Git and ESLint.
- Lobby entry adapters validate strict v1 intent contracts and rate-limit mutations plus lobby-fenced reads before body or database work using an authenticated proxy marker, hashed requester identities, and bounded per-operation storage. Replayed entry commands decode the complete original allowlisted projection without minting credentials, rejoin command persistence and activation share one lock-time lobby transaction, and snapshots authenticate/project in one fenced actor-scoped query that excludes unrelated departed history while preserving the 25-player round plus one waiting replacement only when that waiting participant is the requester.
- Next App Router API modules forward supported methods, unsupported methods, and unknown private catch-all paths to the shared versioned dispatcher so stable JSON errors and `no-store` headers survive the framework routing boundary.
- Authoritative snapshot projections construct stage-specific fields only for stages that require them; an open co-winner window may contain confirmed winners before a settled result exists.
- Framework-routing guarantees require live Next request coverage under an approved migrated `TEST_DATABASE_URL`; dispatcher unit tests and route-source assertions do not prove unsupported methods or catch-all resources retain stable errors and private cache headers.
- Realtime tickets use 32 random bytes encoded as canonical unpadded base64url, persist only SHA-256 hashes bound to lobby/participant/session scope, and issue under the lobby fence from an active cookie session. Consumption burns the presented row whether valid or not and returns only authoritative identity for a valid unexpired active scope; issuance purges expired abandoned tickets, and session deactivation invalidates outstanding tickets so rejoin cannot revive them.
- Round-control commands are rate-limited before lobby-fence acquisition, then resolve the active session, actor role, current round, and own card inside one Serializable transaction; command results persist canonical intent so changed-payload command-ID reuse is rejected, active-lobby replays retain their original sequence, and private mark acknowledgements allocate no lobby sequence. Expire due participant sessions under that fence before selecting a replacement-round roster or deciding whether an absence generation is still current, and detach prior active-event and command-result round scopes so replay tombstones survive without retaining old gameplay state.
- Socket.IO accepts only strict versioned handshake auth from the configured exact browser origin, burns any canonical ticket reaching auth even in an invalid envelope, discards handshake plaintext, stores only persistence-returned identity in `socket.data`, and revalidates that identity inside command/snapshot lobby fences and before later room delivery. Engine.IO admission and namespace authentication have separate bounded direct-peer limits; mark a rejected transport terminal before awaiting its bounded ticket burn, close it, cap authenticated sockets globally and per session, and recheck both transport closure and transport-wide rejection after ticket consumption before reserving capacity or calling `next()`. Every command attempt is charged before the one-in-flight guard, and per-lobby delivery queues preserve committed sequence order through asynchronous authorization while authorizing each unique persisted identity once per delivery. Active-lobby commits emit a transaction-scoped PostgreSQL notification; the separate game-server process serially reloads and validates each committed event before sequence-deduplicated publication, so HTTP fallback mutations reach connected clients without pre-commit effects. Validate every successful acknowledgement's command ID against the incoming mutation before any delivery; fresh committed lobby events broadcast before requester acknowledgements, replays do not rebroadcast, eventless replay tombstones can acknowledge either delivery scope, and replayed private results return only to the requesting socket. Disconnect sockets on terminal command-time identity outcomes (`UNAUTHORIZED`, inactive/deleted-lobby `NOT_FOUND`, or `LOBBY_EXPIRED`) so stale clients cannot retain rooms or capacity.
- Active-event subscription, malformed dedicated-channel notification, durable reload, or relay failure is fatal to the game-server runtime because `LISTEN` recovery cannot prove continuity without a durable cursor. Stop Socket.IO before awaiting subscription/database drain so a stalled delivery cannot keep a continuity-lost authority serving, and settle runtime completion with a safe failure if cleanup fails. Exact direct/notification echoes are idempotent only when their canonical event identity matches bounded recent delivery history; same-sequence conflicts and unknown stale deliveries fail closed.
- Authenticated sockets establish an actor-scoped snapshot baseline before live delivery: join authorized rooms first, buffer a bounded combined set of lobby/private events during the query, emit the snapshot, discard buffered lobby sequences at or below its baseline, then release newer events; every ready-state lobby delivery must also suppress sequences at or below that baseline even when it was queued before synchronization but began socket delivery afterward. Explicit resync uses the same boundary and restores the prior safe baseline plus buffered deliveries after transient query failure; failed initialization disconnects and executes no commands.
- Realtime presence uses the lobby fence and durable participant connection count: the first socket ends the prior absence and creates a connected generation plus sequenced event, extra tabs update only the count, and non-final closes decrement only the count. The final close disconnects the canonical active session, fixes its rejoin deadline, invalidates tickets, and commits a configured durable grace lease; the authority restores a fail-closed bounded lease set after restart and limits concurrent expiry transactions. Generation-fenced expiry returns `expired`, `too-early`, or `stale`, retries only the persistence-authoritative early result, and commits absence before any required pause event. Reconnect or participant departure retires old leases without resuming, host absence takes pause-reason precedence, and resume stays blocked while a current non-overridden absence remains. Cleanup or timer persistence failure is fatal to the supervised authority and must latch on the original persistence promise before sibling authority continuations can run.
- Active-round joins persist as waiting participants with no current card or marks and retain authorized presence/snapshot visibility; their absence does not pause or block current play until replacement-round creation atomically promotes eligible participants to playing and assigns new cards.
- Automatic-call timers are bounded process-local wakeups for exact persisted `(lobbyId, roundId, deadline)` leases; timer and host calls share the Serializable lobby fence and call-commit primitive, every committed lobby event reconciles the next lease, and restart recovery subscribes to durable events before loading leases so stale callbacks cannot repeat a draw position. Generation-fence overlapping per-lobby lease reads, run at most one persistence execution per lobby, retain only its latest queued replacement so stale completions cannot replace current work or starve other lobbies, latch scheduler failures as terminal before draining or reconciling more work, and recheck terminal/closed state after asynchronous recovery before binding.
- Fake-timer race tests must bound deferred coordination with real timer functions captured before fake timers are installed, release every blocker in `finally`, and await in-flight harness/publication cleanup so a failed synchronization assertion cannot hang or poison later tests.
- Pattern progress evaluates every canonical mask from authoritative called/marked cell projections, excludes the free center from required counts, uses canonical mask order for deterministic flexible-rule ties, and treats near-win as exactly one required called-but-unmarked cell while keeping feedback gating separate from completion.
- Participant-private mutations persist a bounded ordered event batch plus its immutable canonical pattern definition, called/marked projection, and feedback decision; a row-level result-format discriminator and integrity digest bind current result JSON to its private row metadata so catalog revisions and coordinated payload rewrites cannot reinterpret replay. Adapters validate the full batch before emitting, fresh commits deliver to the participant room, replays deliver only to the requesting socket, and replacement rounds strip private payload/context plus integrity while retaining intent-only tombstones.
- Co-winner settlement uses an exact persisted `(lobbyId, roundId, triggeringCallId, deadline)` lease with bounded fail-closed scheduling. Only an incomplete-to-complete mark of the latest called ball opens or joins the exclusive-deadline window; the first mark persists one integrity-bound mixed lobby/private result, and settlement orders the complete durable winner set by participant ID before one sequenced broadcast.
- One Line stage continuation updates the same durable round in place through Two Lines and Blackout: preserve cards/marks, calls, and private draw order; replace prior stage winners with only latest-ball completions that also satisfy the next pattern; and leave `nextCallAt` null when all draw positions are already called.
- Inactive-lobby cleanup uses bounded candidate scans only as hints, revalidates the configured threshold plus active-call/connection protection under the Serializable lobby fence with lock-time sampling, and deletes only the lobby parent so PostgreSQL cascades all owned private state. The game server sweeps before lease recovery, runs nonoverlapping periodic cleanup, and treats cleanup failure as fatal; successful join, rejoin, connection, heartbeat, and sequenced presence transitions advance activity with `GREATEST`.
- Shared framework-neutral controls live in `packages/ui`; Next-specific adapters and the atoms/molecules/organisms/templates/lib alias barrels live under `apps/web/src`, with matching app/root TypeScript paths and `react-jsx` so both Next builds and Vitest-imported app TSX resolve consistently.
- After removing a temporary App Router browser harness, run the final production Next build before typecheck so generated `.next/types` no longer reference deleted preview pages, then restore any unrelated `next-env.d.ts` working-tree side effect without staging it.
- Multi-step browser entry flows allocate one stable command ID per persisted step, prevent duplicate submission, retain completed-step state after partial failure, and retry only the unfinished command; public landing metadata and pattern choices derive from the same visible/canonical source rather than duplicate browser data.
- Browser mutation clients treat non-success responses as definitive only when a strict error contract correlates to the outgoing command ID; malformed, missing-ID, and mismatched-ID responses remain ambiguous and replay through the original command session.
- Status-driven forms may move focus into newly revealed controls only when focus remains within the form or was removed with the prior control; asynchronous refreshes must preserve focus that the user moved to another workflow.
- Verify private App Router document cache headers with a production Next server; development mode rewrites document responses to `no-cache, must-revalidate` even when the production route proxy emits `no-store`.
- After a browser mutation acknowledgement, serialize any mandatory snapshot reconciliation behind an in-flight refresh, require the snapshot sequence and expected projection to include the commit, and keep stale controls latched until authority confirms the transition.
- Card mark clients accept both participant-private acknowledgements and active-lobby acknowledgements because a winning mark can open the co-winner window; reconcile the authoritative own mark against the same card and require a lobby sequence only for active-lobby scope.
- Browser live projections apply only contiguous lobby events, ignore stale duplicates, reject lower-sequence snapshots, validate every locally projected snapshot, and request one resync for gaps or inconsistent references; automatic call events update the visible call immediately but require a snapshot to restore the next authoritative deadline without replaying call-history announcements. Participant-private marks carry no lobby sequence, so merge them append-only only within the same card and preserve them across equal-sequence snapshots.
- Browser realtime adapters retry transient ticket, handshake, and retryable server failures with bounded delays and a fresh single-use ticket; strict non-retryable ticket errors terminate in an explicit expired state rather than looping or reusing credentials.
- Replayable browser commands retain their original pre-command reconciliation baseline because live state may already include an ambiguous first attempt before its same-ID replay acknowledgement arrives.
- Retained round commands stay bound to their original round, while absence overrides stay bound to an exact participant presence generation; recheck the latest authoritative snapshot both when it arrives and after an ambiguous response, and treat a later lobby sequence as proof that an acknowledged command was included even when the state has since advanced.
- When authoritative updates remove or disable focused controls, recover focus after the render based on meaningful control/outcome availability rather than only stage changes; keep card focus while co-winner marks remain valid, move it when settlement locks the card, and let the native dialog cancel event own Escape handling.
- Outcome views derive complete winner names and window duration only from the authoritative snapshot plus authorized roster, keep the open co-winner window distinct from settled results, and bind transient live announcements to an exact round/pattern/window/result identity across HTTP and realtime snapshot acceptance so unrelated events preserve them, changed outcomes clear them, and reconnect snapshots restore visible results silently.
- Long-lived browser realtime handlers read current readiness from refs rather than render-time closures; when outcome layout changes reading order, keep announcement nodes mounted and reorder only visible panels.
- Responsive decorative wordmarks need browser-level bounding checks based on rendered content width, not only the grid item's box; reserve an explicit track plus readable separation at the breakpoint where multi-column layout begins.
- Public privacy/lifecycle copy receives only allowlisted runtime duration values from the server entry point; definitive session/lobby errors latch all snapshot and realtime delivery closed, while an unavailable-lobby view must discard the old locator/private content, focus its terminal heading once, and link only to fresh create/join flows.
- Theme visual assets are canonical theme metadata rendered into one external SVG sprite per theme; generate sprites and review documents with `bun scripts/generate-theme-assets.ts`, preload only the selected lobby sprite, and keep every SVG decorative, unfocusable, static-capable, and backed by semantic HTML plus a load-failure fallback.
- Project-original theme audio uses canonical cue metadata and one generated mono PCM WAV sprite per theme; create/resume browser audio only from explicit opt-in, fetch only the selected theme, persist only validated mute/volume preferences, and trigger cues only from fresh authoritative events rather than snapshots.
- Keep tracked media in one canonical inventory that generates `docs/assets.md`; enforce aggregate selected-theme visual/audio budgets, bind nongenerated provenance to content digests, and add AVIF/WebP only when an approved raster source actually exists.
- Full-stack Playwright journeys start both the production Next server and game-server authority against a dedicated migrated browser-test database; require `E2E_DATABASE_CONFIRMED_NONPRODUCTION=true`, run one matrix project per invocation, and do not share that database concurrently or sequentially with repository integration suites whose final capacity fixtures may intentionally remain committed.
- Keep the default Playwright project portable and enable the complete desktop/mobile engine set with `PLAYWRIGHT_BROWSER_MATRIX=all`; document native Safari/mobile and retained previous-stable coverage separately because WebKit and device emulation are not native execution.
- Serialize Node Vitest files that share `TEST_DATABASE_URL`; PostgreSQL repository cleanup and Socket.IO database-backed recovery tests cannot safely run against the same database concurrently.
- The production-mode Playwright harness serves HTTP, so WebKit cannot carry the required `Secure` participant cookie there; run its noncredential checks locally and assign the authenticated Safari/iOS Safari journey to the release owner over production-like HTTPS rather than weakening cookie security.
- Accessibility regressions combine state-focused React Testing Library coverage with browser Axe scans; derive the complete cross-theme semantic/visual matrix from canonical generated moodboards, keep Chromium screenshot baselines scoped to stable nontext artwork, and exercise real private-lobby states plus asset failures in every credential-capable browser project.
- HTTP mutations compare `Origin` with canonical `WEB_ORIGIN`, require the shared `x-gamenight-request: mutation` JSON header, reject query parameters and malformed UTF-8 before persistence, and validate catalog-backed selections before creating durable state; private responses share no-store, noindex, framing, MIME, permissions, referrer, and per-request nonce CSP protections without `unsafe-inline` scripts.
- Socket.IO payload-cap regressions should verify all three transport boundaries: a valid below-cap packet reaches its handler, a near-cap packet reaches application validation, and an oversized packet disconnects before command execution; assert serialized packet sizes so fixture drift cannot invalidate the boundary evidence.
- Single-instance performance evidence uses a fresh empty migrated database, derives the fixed 100-lobby/25-participant profile from runtime defaults, staggers lobby calls at the fastest supported automatic cadence, validates exact per-client events and actor snapshots, and writes ignored percentile evidence under `test-results`; never share that retained database with Vitest or browser suites.
- Keep `/healthz` independent of PostgreSQL and implement `/readyz` with a bounded, coalesced, briefly cached database probe that retains ownership of timed-out work until it settles; derive database-dependent API handlers lazily so readiness can observe startup rejection without creating an unhandled secondary promise, and cache the operational logger with the global database/readiness state so retry and command contexts remain aligned across module reevaluation. Structured operational diagnostics use typed allowlisted scalar records, hash all client-controlled identifiers plus lobby/participant correlations, propagate hashed command context to command-driven transaction retries, log only fresh sequenced deliveries rather than exact echoes, adapt committed acknowledgements at the wire boundary, record terminal disconnect-pause failures, permanently drop output after an asynchronous stream error, and never serialize requests, commands, events, errors, snapshots, cards, credentials, or future draw data.

  - Kept Playwright separate from Vitest and used a runner-only smoke because no application runtime or browser journey exists yet; browser binaries were not installed outside the worktree.
  - Added a root `tsconfig.json` that checks repository source, tests, and typed configs because the mandated plain `npx tsc --noEmit` hook must not become a no-op.
  - Made `bun run test` execute the complete root/workspace typecheck before Vitest so the exact hook still enforces each workspace's narrower ambient type environment.
  - Preserved the exact required bare-`npx` hook commands despite the review's network-fallback concern because changing those bytes would violate the acceptance criterion; pinned local `lint-staged` and TypeScript binaries provide the normal resolution path.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Custom Vitest project `include` patterns must be rooted to repository-owned paths or dependency and `.opencode` tests can be collected despite normal defaults.
  - Intentional failure fixtures should assert stable diagnostic markers, not merely nonzero status, and must stay outside normal lint, format, typecheck, Vitest, and Playwright discovery.
  - A fixture TypeScript config that extends the root must explicitly override the root fixture exclusion while retaining inherited `noEmit`; otherwise it proves only a no-input configuration error or can emit generated JavaScript.
  - Playwright tests that do not request a browser fixture can validate runner wiring before product browser journeys and browser installation are available.
- Known issues / follow-ups:
  - Browser-backed Playwright journeys and their required browser binaries remain owned by later frontend/test-suite stories.
  - Product React/Next.js runtime dependencies and application scripts remain owned by later dependency-ordered stories.
- Next iteration start:
  - Implement US-008 runtime configuration defaults, overrides, validation, and startup tests without allowing domain code to read process environment directly.

  - The same injected byte-source and rejection-sampling convention should be reused for the draw-order shuffle in US-012.

  - Runtime adapters that supply secure bytes land in later application stories; the domain intentionally requires the source as an argument.

- Decisions (why):
  - Reused the existing command-result primary key, event foreign key, and lobby sequence column without a migration because they already enforce the required durable relationships.
  - Used a no-op lobby-row write before the idempotency lookup so all mutations for one lobby have one serializable ordering point, including participant-private commands that otherwise change no lobby state.
  - Scoped the callback repository to the target lobby and returned a broadcastable event only for a fresh active-lobby commit so callers cannot publish before commit, rebroadcast replays, or create sequence gaps for private results.
  - Required a caller-provided result decoder and rejected command-type/round mismatches on replay so persisted JSON is never cast to a newly inferred handler result type.
  - Used deterministic capped backoff rather than jitter because the single-instance MVP has bounded lobby contention and deterministic injected sleep makes retry behavior directly testable.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Prisma 7 surfaces raw PostgreSQL serialization failures as `P2010` errors with SQLSTATE `40001` nested in adapter metadata, while other write conflicts may use top-level `P2034`; retry classification must handle both without broadly retrying integrity failures.
  - Serializable callbacks can execute more than once after rolled-back conflicts, so IDs, timestamps, randomness, and external effects must be prepared outside the callback or persisted through its transaction-scoped repositories.
  - Replayed and participant-private commits deliberately return `committedEvent: null`; only a fresh active-lobby commit is safe to broadcast.
- Known issues / follow-ups:
  - Root `bun run format:check` still scans three pre-existing untracked US-018 report files; they remain untouched and unstaged, while the complete intended candidate passes Prettier.

- Decisions (why):

  - Used 32 random bytes, unpadded base64url, and SHA-256 because a uniformly random 256-bit bearer credential does not need a password KDF; the plaintext exists only in the returned cookie descriptor.
  - Used a `__Secure-` cookie with no Domain, no persistent expiry, SameSite=Strict, and a per-lobby API path because `__Host-` would require the broader root path and the product has not defined persistent cookie retention.
  - Added no migration because the committed schema already enforces a 32-byte unique digest, lobby/participant ownership, lifecycle consistency, and lobby-owned cascade deletion.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Hash the encoded credential rather than raw entropy so issuance and cookie resolution use one canonical representation, and reject malformed/noncanonical tokens before querying persistence.
  - Session authentication should return only the scoped identity projection needed by adapters; loading `findById` would unnecessarily expose all session hashes and private lobby state to an authentication path.
  - Generate credentials outside retryable persistence callbacks, classify only the exact token-hash unique violation as a regenerable collision, and let unrelated integrity failures propagate.
- Known issues / follow-ups:
  - Root `bun run format:check` still scans three pre-existing untracked US-018 report files; they remain untouched and unstaged, while every intended story file passes Prettier.

- Decisions (why):
  - Returned original entry/session metadata with no `Set-Cookie` on replay because a public command ID can support idempotent result retrieval but cannot prove participant identity or authorize credential issuance.
  - Stored the complete allowlisted original entry projection inside the private command result rather than adding schema columns because mutable participant/lobby rows cannot reconstruct an immutable replay and no migration is needed.
  - Used one transaction for valid-cookie rejoin instead of composing status, command, and activation calls because expiry or command conflicts must roll back without partially activating or recording the session.
  - Allowed 26 snapshot participants only for the maximum 25-player round plus the requesting waiting replacement because all referenced winners, the host, and self must remain representable while durable departed history stays bounded out of the projection.
  - Required a secret proxy marker before accepting the rightmost forwarded address and hashed it before storage; direct, invalid, or unauthenticated headers share a bounded fallback rather than creating attacker-controlled keys.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Entry-command idempotency records must retain immutable response metadata, but credential issuance always requires separate scoped proof of identity.
  - Rejoin command persistence, expiry, activation, and sibling invalidation are one lifecycle transition and must share one lobby fence and sampled lock-time clock.
  - Snapshot collection bounds must account for required historical references in addition to current admission capacity; one waiting replacement can coexist with a full prior-round winner roster.
  - Process-local limiter maps need both trusted requester normalization and a hard active-bucket bound; expiry cleanup alone does not prevent active-key memory growth.

  - The unrelated untracked US-018 browser reports remain untouched and unstaged; root `bun run format:check` continues to scan three of them while every tracked file passes Prettier.

- The full-stack keyboard journey programmatically focuses most controls and uses pointer clicks for navigation/refresh, so it does not prove natural Tab/Shift+Tab reachability across the complete create/join/lobby/card/host/result flow.

- These are accepted blocking findings because they directly affect US-058's every-theme production-state, asset-failure, keyboard, and portable visual-regression acceptance. Per the one-targeted-re-review limit, no further implementation changes or commit are permitted in this iteration.

  - Staggered the 100 lobby commands by 50 ms with a rotating phase because this models the maximum normal automatic cadence of one call per lobby every five seconds; an initial synchronized 100-command spike exceeded the bounded transaction retry envelope and is not the PRD's normal latency profile.
  - Kept fixture joins and connection establishment serial because they are outside the measured workload and parallel setup manufactured unrelated Serializable conflicts before load measurement.
  - Recorded browser render completion in the harness process after two animation frames so commit-to-render uses one monotonic clock and conservatively includes the Playwright callback hop.
  - Derived capacity from `RUNTIME_CONFIG_DEFAULTS` and included the executable script in root TypeScript coverage so configuration drift or harness type errors fail normal checks.
  - Retained failed and successful local test databases without destructive cleanup; every acceptance attempt used an empty migrated database and never reused partial load state.
  - Testing decision: this story primarily adds test infrastructure and acceptance evidence; the pre-existing candidate shutdown regression covered its production close-idempotency fix, and all harness behavior is directly exercised by focused tests plus the full gated run.
- **Learnings for future iterations:**
  - Capacity setup and capacity workload are separate concerns: serial fixture setup avoids measuring retry noise that normal gameplay does not create, while rotating phased commands exercise the intended steady-state arrival rate without best-case browser ordering.
  - Browser timestamps should cross into the load-generator clock at observation time rather than subtracting independent process clocks; two animation frames provide a conservative rendered-state boundary.
  - Heavy harnesses must fail on integrity and cleanup as well as latency, typecheck with the repository, and keep generated reports ignored rather than committing machine-specific benchmark artifacts.
- Known issues / follow-ups:
  - The harness measures one realtime authority in the same Bun process as its Node load clients; process isolation and CPU/RSS/event-loop telemetry are useful future capacity refinements but are not required for the measured MVP acceptance threshold.
  - Four retained local nonproduction performance databases and separate check/E2E databases were not deleted because destructive local data cleanup was not required.
  - Root `bun run format:check` remains blocked by unrelated pre-existing `.playwright-mcp` artifacts; every tracked file passes Prettier.
- Next iteration start:
  - If review passes, implement US-061 health/readiness and privacy-safe logging; otherwise remediate merged blocking performance or test findings within the one-re-review limit.
